    Comprehensive Collection of Ancient and Modern Books, Volume 155

    Tooth Gate

    Huangdi's Suwen

    On the Ancient Heavenly Truths

    At seven years old, a girl's kidney energy is strong, and her teeth grow longer. At three times seven, kidney energy is balanced, hence true teeth grow and become very long.
    [Note: For a girl at seven, the kidney energy is robust. The kidneys govern the bones, and teeth are extensions of the bones, so the teeth grow longer. True teeth are those that fully develop; with sufficient kidney energy, true teeth grow.]

    At eight years old, a boy's kidney energy is solid, hair grows longer and teeth grow. At three times eight, kidney energy is balanced, tendons and bones are strong, so true teeth grow and become very long. At five times eight, kidney energy declines, hair falls out and teeth become brittle. By eight times eight, teeth and hair fall away.
    [Note: True teeth grow strong and bones develop to their utmost. The kidneys are the source of life energy; for boys, when energy declines, at five times eight, the foundational energy begins to weaken, leading to hair loss and brittle teeth. By eight times eight, energy declines to a critical level, resulting in loss.]

    Essential Diagnosis Conclusion

    If Shaoyin ends, the face is dark, teeth are long and stained, the abdomen is bloated and blocked, unable to communicate above and below, thus it ends.
    [Note: The brilliance of the heart resides in the face. The darkness indicates an excess of water energy, while fire energy is diminished, leading to the escape of water energy. Long and stained teeth indicate a depletion of bone energy. A bloated abdomen and blockage, unable to communicate above and below, indicate the exhaustion of both heart and kidney energies, preventing vertical circulation.][1p]
    On the Correspondence of Yin and Yang

    Qibo said: When yang is abundant, the body becomes hot, the pores are closed, breathing is rough, and one struggles to breathe with movements up and down. Sweating does not occur, yet there is heat, the teeth become dry and one feels vexed and grievance, the abdomen is full, leading to death. One can endure in winter but not in summer.

    Note: When yang prevails, it signifies the heat of fire, hence the body is hot. Heat on the surface results in closed pores; heat within causes rough breathing. When yin prevails in the abdomen, it causes downward movement; when yang prevails in the back, it causes upward movement. When yang dominates the whole body, there is no sweating and there is heat. The kidneys govern essence, hence the teeth become dry as the essence is depleted. The heart governs blood; hence one feels vexed as the blood is exhausted. A full abdomen indicates that the vital energy of the middle burner is completely depleted. This is the manifestation of death due to excessive yang heat. However, one can prolong existence in winter but cannot escape in summer.

    On Atrophy

    Those with kidney heat have dark coloration and decayed teeth.

    The emperor said: A person suffers from headache for several years, how could this arise, and what is it called? Qibo replied: It arises from having been subjected to extreme cold, penetrating to the marrow. The marrow is dominated by the brain; when the marrow rebels, it causes headache and also tooth pain, the condition is named reversal of qi.

    Note: The kidneys produce marrow, hence being affected by the cold results in it penetrating to the marrow. All marrow is related to the brain, thus the brain is fundamental. When the inverted evil of the marrow rises, it enters the brain, which is why the headache persists for several years. The teeth are the remnants of bone, which is why they also ache. This cold penetrates below and rebels upward to the summit, thus it is named reversal of qi.[2p]
    The Essential Discourse on True Reality

    In the year of the Yin, in the season of spring, heat prevails and overpowers. The people suffer from constant sounds in their abdomen, with Qi rising up to the chest, leading to breathing difficulties and inability to stand for long. They experience cold and heat, skin pain, closed eyes, toothaches, and swelling.

    Note: The Yin in spring refers to the year of the rabbit or rooster. The constant sounds in the abdomen indicate excessive fire energy. Qi rising to the chest suggests that the fire energy ascends. Breathing difficulties, inability to stand for long, cold and heat, and skin pain indicate that excessive fire is affecting the lungs and metal element. Closed eyes signify severe heat and Yin deficiency, leading to a sensitivity to sunlight. Toothaches and swelling indicate that heat affects the Yangming channel.

    Lingshu Classic

    Meridian Chapter

    The Yangming meridian of the hand has a branch that runs from the clavicle, through the neck, and into the cheeks, entering the lower teeth. The Yangming meridian of the foot travels down the outside of the nose and enters the upper teeth.

    Evil Invaders Chapter

    In the heavens, there are constellations; on earth, there are teeth.[3p]
    Bian Que's Difficult Classics

    Diagnosis of Death

    If a patient's lips are swollen and teeth are decayed, the patient will die; the spleen and kidneys are exhausted.
    If a patient's teeth suddenly turn black, they will die in thirteen days; the lesser yin is exhausted.
    Zhong Cang Jing [Han Dynasty, Hua Tuo]

    Diagnosis of Death

    If the stomach is exhausted, and the teeth fall out with a yellow face, the patient will die in seven days. [Some say ten days.] A face lacking luster with black teeth will die.
    If teeth suddenly become black, they will die in thirteen days.

    Qian Jin Fang [Tang Dynasty, Sun Simiao]

    Discussion

    In general, when the gums are exposed, it is often due to malnutrition (with worms residing above and below) and lunar eclipses. Applying the ash of grassy plants to the gums at night ensures full recovery; do not eat oil; one or two nights will suffice. Eating oil and dried dates can exacerbate the condition. Thus, those suffering from dental issues should avoid oil, dried dates, and cinnamon bark. Each morning, take a pinch of salt in the mouth, gargle with warm water, and brush the teeth, tapping them a hundred times. This should not take more than five days for the mouth and teeth to stabilize. If a person is unable to eat fruits and vegetables due to exposed tooth roots, this saltwater method of cleaning and tapping the teeth will surely cure them. Many people who suffer from dental diseases often do so due to eating or drinking during lunar eclipses, so the knowledgeable should be cautious. Therefore, during eclipses of the sun and moon, it is especially advisable to avoid eating and drinking, including for young children.[4p]
    Direct Pointer to Ren Zhai
    [Song Dynasty, Yang Shiying]

    Teeth and the Kidneys
    Teeth are the end of the bones and are nourished by the marrow; thus, the kidneys are primarily responsible for them. Therefore, when the kidneys weaken, the teeth become loose; when the essence is abundant, the teeth are strong; and when there is deficiency heat, the teeth become unstable.

    Toxin Phlegm Pain
    Heat produces phlegm, which attacks with toxic gases, filling the channels and causing pain. For outward symptoms of abundant phlegm with coughing and spitting, it is suitable to use Er Chen Tang combined with Xi Xin, Zhi Ke, fresh ginger, Da Zao, and Wu Mei decocted. Additionally, use turmeric and Piper longum decocted together, wait until warm, and immerse the tongue in the decoction to allow saliva to flow out, which is effective.

    Insect Erosion Pain
    When individuals do not maintain clean teeth while eating, the foul-smelling gases accumulate over time, causing the gums to have holes where insects erode the teeth. If one tooth is eroded completely, the others will worsen, leading to conditions like gnawing (hidden internal insects). It is essential to eliminate the insects to stop the pain.[5p]
    Causes of Pain

    The branches of the Yangming hand channel enter the teeth; if blocked, the teeth feel loose; if empty, they show signs of exposure; if wind accompanies, it attacks the head and face; if there is consumption, it leads to decay.

    Tooth Abscess

    If a lump the size of a bean appears by the tooth, it is due to fire from the spleen and stomach channels. It is advisable to use a small knife to pierce it, apply Borneol powder, and then take Clear Stomach Decoction or Sweet Tangerine Decoction, all will heal.

    Tooth Swelling

    The teeth are associated with the kidney channel; this condition may arise from wind entering through deficiency, excess drinking causing swelling, blood deficiency causing swelling, injury causing swelling, or sexual exhaustion leading to kidney deficiency causing swelling. The treatment should be tailored based on the specific symptoms.

    Tooth Exposed

    Tooth exposure refers to heat surging from the spleen and stomach. In this condition, bleeding occurs between the teeth, associated with the spleen above and the stomach below. If there is difficulty treating blood-tinged phlegm that is abundant, urgent treatment is needed, as delay may lead to severe consequences. First, cleanse with clam water, then blow in the medication.

    Cold Entering the Brain and Causing Pain

    Kidney deficiency leading to great cold results in headaches and tooth pain, which, if severe and persistent for years, indicates this condition; it can be treated with Tian Nan Xing pills.[6p]
    Pain Belongs to Fire

    Some individuals experience pain in their upper and lower teeth; whenever pain arises, they promptly remove them. Not long later, all their teeth are gone. By the age of fifty, they can no longer eat hard substances. The pain in the upper and lower teeth is caused by excessive wind and heat in the Yangming meridians of the hands and feet. One can use medicines like Da and Xiao Chengqi Decoction, Zangyong Pills, or Qu Feng Pills to purge them, and then the pain should naturally stop. The Inner Canon states that all pains, itching, sores, and ulcers are associated with heart fire. Wang Bing said: All origins arise from the heart. The heart represents fire; fire gives rise to earth. It is important to understand the reasons for tooth emergence.

    Wind Pain

    For those suffering from tooth pain due to wind excess that does not heal over time, one can insert a single Ba Dou seed into the flame and let it emit smoke. Before it loses its potency, smoke it over the root of the tooth; this will bring healing.
    — Dongyuan’s Ten Treatises [Yuan Dynasty, Li Gao]

    Discussion

    Teeth are markers of the kidneys, while the mouth is the opening of the spleen. Many meridians converge around the mouth; the teeth are where the Yangming meridians of both hands and feet pass through. The upper gums belong to the Earth and are connected to the meridian of the Stomach in the foot Yangming, which remains still and motionless. The lower gums chew food, moving continuously; this is connected to the meridian of the Large Intestine in the hand Yangming. The hand Yangming dislikes cold drinks and prefers warmth, whereas the foot Yangming enjoys cold drinks and dislikes heat; hence, their illnesses differ. The teeth, as indicators of kidney health, also prefer cold; cold makes them strong. When heat accumulates, the teeth become loose, and pain persists, which is why treatments vary.[7p]
    There are those who experience pain from aversion to heat, and those who experience pain from aversion to cold; some suffer pain from both aversion to cold and heat. There are others who, when drinking little cold and much hot, experience pain, and those who, when drinking little hot and much cold, also experience pain. Some have loose teeth that cause pain; some have cavities that cause pain; others have gums eroded by decay, bleeding and causing pain, while some have swollen gums that cause pain. Additionally, if there is wind-evil in the spleen and stomach, one may feel pain from just the wind. There are also those whose teeth are heavily decayed by worms, leading to loss and color change, resulting in toothache from decayed teeth; others have poor stomach energy unable to endure the cold, with exposed teeth causing pain. Moreover, there are those with painful teeth that emit a foul odor deterring closeness. Since pain is not uniform, can one medicine resolve all?

    When there is excess heat in the stomach and pain in the upper teeth is particularly severe, it is advisable to use Liangge Powder. Steep rhubarb with wine as the main ingredient, add Anemarrhena, gypsum, and Cimicifuga as assistants, and frequently hold and swallow it to recover.

    For those who slightly dislike cold drinks but greatly dislike hot drinks, it is best to use Lixiao Powder.[8p]
    Heat Pain

    Heat pain occurs when there is excess heat in the intestines and stomach, leading to swollen gums and foul breath. It is advisable to use Cool Diaphragm Powder with additions of Anemarrhena, Gypsum, and Cimicifuga. Use wine-steamed Rhubarb as the primary ingredient; simply swish and swallow to heal.

    Pain Associated with Heat

    Tooth pain arises when damp heat in the stomach rises and affects the gums, especially when obstructed by wind-cold or cold food, preventing the damp heat from dissipating, thus causing pain. Cold is the symptom, so use warm and stimulating topical treatments; heat is the root cause, so take warming and cooling internal medications. For toothache, use Wutong Tears powdered with a little Musk rubbed on. For severe tooth pain, use Pepper and Piper cubeba to disperse superficial heat, supplemented with Cimicifuga and Huai Shi, assisted by warming cooling herbs like Schizonepeta, Mint, and Asarum. Using purely cooling herbs may prevent the pain from resolving. Treatment must be targeted, using species such as Piper cubeba, Chuanxiong, Mint, Schizonepeta, Asarum, Camphor, and coarse salt.[9p]
    Medical Correct Transmission
    (Ming - Yu Tuan)

    Discussion

    The "Inner Canon" states: the onset of hundreds of diseases stems from both fundamental and superficial causes. The teeth are external signs of the kidneys, and remnants of the bones. The stomach's Yangming channel connects to the gums above the teeth; the Yangming channel of the large intestine connects to the gums below the teeth. The hand's Yangming dislikes cold drinks and prefers hot ones, while the foot's Yangming dislikes hot drinks and prefers cold ones, which explains the different types of pain they experience related to cold and heat. If one opens their mouth and feels exacerbated pain, it indicates an invasion of wind evil in the intestines and stomach; if the breath becomes foul and unbearable upon opening the mouth, it indicates accumulated heat in the intestines and stomach. There are cases where pain causes the teeth to loosen, or pain leads to tooth decay, or gaps between teeth inhibit eating—all of these are related. Generally, if the gums are receding and the teeth are loose, it indicates a deficiency in the kidney essence; the treatment should focus on nourishing Yin and supplementing the kidneys. If there is aversion to cold and a strong heat sensation along with foul breath, it indicates excessive heat in the stomach; the treatment should focus on calming the stomach and draining fire. The so-called evidence of wind evil and insect infestation is essentially due to heat generating wind, which in turn generates insects. If the fire in the intestines and stomach is subdued, and additional measures are taken to cleanse the teeth and eliminate insects, there will inevitably be tranquility in treatment.[10p]
    Essentials of Diagnosis and Treatment (Ming Dynasty, Dai Sigong)

    Tooth Pain

    Tooth pain can be caused by wind, toxins, or heat obstruction, tooth decay, and kidney deficiency. If the exact condition is not identified, it is advisable to use a dispersing powder for wind and toxins applied topically. For all conditions, it is appropriate to use three parts of fried sweet fennel and one part of fried salt, ground together for regular application. If tooth worms have emerged, and the cavity is hollow and painful, this is crucial to recognize. It is advisable to use a small amount of frankincense, heated until soft to fill the cavity. If kidney deficiency leads to floating and painful teeth, particularly if there is aversion to cold and a feeling of internal heat, it may present symptoms similar to wanting to fall out. In such cases, it is beneficial to use kidney nourishing pills and intermittently take black tin pills.

    Compendium of Materia Medica (Ming Dynasty, Li Shizhen)

    Eating Sour Foods Makes Teeth Soft

    People from Chu often eat sour foods, resulting in soft teeth. This is because the water generates wood; with weakened moisture and strong wood element, the teeth are affected in this way.

    Miscellaneous Medical Writings (Ming Dynasty, Wang Luan)

    Swollen and Painful Gums[11p]
    Swollen and painful gums, tooth pain with looseness, or blackening and falling out of teeth; the world commonly treats this as kidney deficiency. Little do they realize this pertains to damp heat in the Yangming channel. Though the teeth belong to the kidneys, they arise from the gums, and the upper and lower gums correlate with the Yangming large intestine and stomach, akin to wood growing from the earth. The intestines and stomach are harmed by fine wines, rich flavors, and greasy, sweet foods, causing damp heat to rise. Consequently, the gums become inflamed and painful, possibly bleeding or infested with worms, leading to the discomfort, looseness, blackening, or loss of teeth. Treatment should focus on dispelling the damp heat of the Yangming, thus clearing and soothing the gums, allowing the teeth to stabilize and strengthen.

    [Note: For tooth pain, if caused by damp heat in the hand and foot Yangming channels, use Dongyuan's Qingwei Powder; if due to wind-cold entering the brain leading to headaches and tooth pain, use Qianghuo Fuzi Xixin Decoction; if caused by excessive thinking damaging the spleen, use Guipi Decoction; if due to accumulated anger, use Yueju Pill; if arising from consumption of alcohol and fried foods, use Qingwei Powder; if related to diet harming the spleen, use Liu Junzi Decoction; if from overexertion damaging original qi, use Buzhong Yiqi Decoction; if the spleen and stomach are inherently weak, use Liu Jun Gui Decoction; if due to kidney yin deficiency, use Liuwei Dihuang Wan; if from kidney yang deficiency, use Bawei Wan; if both yin and yang are deficient, use Shibu Wan; if there is spleen and kidney deficiency with cold, use Anshen Wan. Mr. Xu Yongcheng remarked: all tooth diseases accompanied by cold or heat symptoms, pertain to the hand and foot Yangming channels; tooth loosening and gum loss, correspond to the foot Shaoyin channel; tooth decay, swelling, pain, and bleeding are all caused by stomach fire. There are also mixed syndromes from various channels and external factors affecting patients.][12p]
    Introduction to Medicine
    [Ming - Li Zhan]

    Stasis Blood Pain
    When wind-heat attacks the gums, causing blood to flow out, phlegm stagnates and does not dissipate, resulting in pulling pain and piercing discomfort. It is advisable to use Xijiao Dihuang Decoction, or a modified version of Ganlu Drink with the addition of Shengma.

    Loose and Shaky Gums
    If the gums are loose and shaky, it indicates kidney essence deficiency. It is advisable to use Eight Treasure Pills to nourish yin and tonify the kidneys.

    Wind-Heat Pain
    In cases of wind-heat, the external wind and internal heat clash, leading to swollen and painful gums with a foul-smelling discharge. It is advisable to use Xijiao Shengma Decoction, along with Jing Jie Decoction for gargling.

    Wind-Cold Pain
    In cases of wind-cold, the gums are neither swollen nor decayed but gradually become loose. It is advisable to use Warm Wind Powder, along with Kai Xiao Powder for gargling.[13p]
    Tooth Decay Pain

    Tooth decay leads to bone exposure and bleeding; in such cases, Yuchi Powder should be used.

    Cold and Heat Sensitivity

    The foot yangming stomach channel enters the upper teeth; this condition prefers cold drinks and despises hot drinks. The hand yangming large intestine channel enters the lower teeth; this condition prefers hot drinks and despises cold drinks. Heat-induced tooth pain fears cold water, cold-induced tooth pain fears hot water; a tooth that fears neither temperature is caused by wind.

    Heat Pain

    If pain arises from damp heat being obstructed by cold wind, Danggui Longdan Powder should be used. For longstanding tooth pain, with black decay and falling out, relief comes from slightly cooling; this is due to the heat of dampness from rich foods. The Stomach Regulating Qi Decoction with added Huanglian should be taken.

    Pulse Diagnosis

    The right Guan pulse is rapid and forceful, or string-like and forceful, indicating wind heat in the intestines and stomach causing pain. The尺 pulse is large and weak, suggesting kidney deficiency, leading to loose and mobile teeth with fiery heat rising and causing pain.

    Pain Diagnosis

    In dental conditions, if there is pain when opening the mouth to let in wind, it indicates wind evil in the stomach; if there is a foul odor when opening the mouth, it indicates accumulated heat in the intestines and stomach; if the root of the tooth is swollen and painful, it indicates stomach heat; if there is pain and mobility, it indicates kidney deficiency; if there are cavities leading to pain, it indicates decay. Upper molar pain relates to deficiency heat in the kidney channel of the foot Shaoyin; use Xiangxintang. Lower molar pain relates to wind and deficiency heat in the hand Yangming; use Baizhitang.[14p]
    Discussion on Dental and Oral Health

    The teeth are a marker of the kidneys, while the mouth is an opening of the spleen. Many meridians converge in the mouth, as seen with the teeth and gums. Mr. Xu Yongcheng states: Teeth are affected by conditions of cold and heat, which pertain to the Yangming meridian of the limbs. Their mobility and loss relate to the Shaoyin meridian of the feet. Cases of tooth decay, gum swelling, bleeding, pain, and foulness are all associated with damp-heat and stomach fire, or the entrenchment of pathogens from various meridians and external factors.

    Treatment methods: For severe damp-heat and pain, administer Chengqi Decoction; for milder cases, use Qīngwèi Powder to regulate it. If there is large intestine heat with swollen, painful gums, apply Qīngwèi Powder; if severe, use Tiáowèi Pill to clear it. For pain due to six stagnations, use Yuèjū Pill to resolve it. If pain is due to deficiency of the central qi, use Bǔzhōng Yìqì Decoction to supplement it. If pain arises from excessive thinking affecting the spleen, use Guīpí Decoction to regulate it. If there is kidney deficiency with heat and pain, use Liùwèihǎo Pill to supplement. If it's kidney deficiency with cold and pain, use Huánshǎo Dān to replenish; in serious cases, employ Bāwèi Pill as the primary treatment. For conditions associated with wind-heat, use Dúhuó Powder. If great cold has invaded the brain, apply Báizhǐ Powder. For wind-cold entering the brain, use Qiānghuó Fùzǐ Decoction. Diseases are numerous, and treatment should be adapted according to the clinical situation.[15p]
    The Six Essentials of Medicine
    By Zhang Sanxi (Ming Dynasty)
    On the Causes of Alcohol and Lust

    The gums belong to the stomach, while the teeth belong to the kidneys. In middle age, excessive indulgence in alcohol and lust weakens the essence, which cannot nourish the teeth. Heavy and toxic wine gradually corrupts the stomach, leading to a polluted state in the gums and teeth; when they are polluted, they decay. This is akin to how a tree falls if the ground is not solid. When the teeth loosen, it suggests imminent loss. Tooth root pain indicates heat in the gums approaching decay. The classics state: at the age of fifty-eight, a man's kidney essence declines, leading to hair loss and tooth decay. Once he reaches forty, if the kidneys have already weakened, how much more will they suffer from great consumption? Those who seek life should not place full blame on medicine.

    Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment
    By Wang Kentang (Ming Dynasty)

    Affiliation of the Teeth

    The teeth are associated with the Foot Shaoyin Kidney Channel.
    (Note: The "Suwen" states: at the age of fifty-eight, a man's kidney essence declines, leading to hair loss and tooth decay. It also says: in cases of kidney heat, the color darkens and teeth decay. For those at the end of the Shaoyin phase, the face is dark, teeth are elongated, and decay occurs.) The teeth are divided into upper and lower gums; the upper gums belong to the Foot Yangming Stomach Channel.[16p]
    The "Su Wen" states that pathogenic factors affecting the foot's Yangming channel can cause nasal bleeding and cold in the upper teeth. The "Zhenjing" mentions that pain in the upper teeth prefers cold and dislikes heat, and that one should apply acupressure to the original point at the Chongyang point, located in the artery between the bones of the feet, five inches above the ankles. Note: '丬' refers to 'judge.' The left half is '丬,' the right half is '片.' Zhu Danxi suggested moxibustion at the Sanli point, which is a major point of the foot's Yangming channel, located on the outer side of the leg, three fingerbreadths below the knees, about a finger's width away from the tibia, between the two tendons.

    The lower gums are related to the hand's Yangming large intestine channel. Zhang Jiegugu stated that Qinjiao can relieve lower tooth pain and eliminate wind and dampness of this channel. The "Zhenjing" states that pain in the lower teeth prefers heat and dislikes cold, thus one should apply acupressure to the original point at the Hegu point, situated in the valley between the first and second metacarpal bones of the hands. Zhu Danxi suggested moxibustion at the Sanjian point, which is a point of the hand's Yangming channel, located in the seam on the inner side of the second phalanx of the thumb and index finger, at the junction of the red and white flesh.

    In boys, at the age of eight, kidney energy is abundant, and the teeth regenerate; by the age of thirty, permanent teeth emerge, by fifty, the teeth begin to decay, and by eighty, they are lost. The same applies to girls, who follow the number seven. The kidneys govern the bones, and teeth are the extensions of the bones, nourished by their marrow, thus correlating with the cycles of heavenly essence. The branches of the foot's Yangming channel enter the upper teeth, while those of the hand's Yangming channel enter the lower teeth. If the marrow of the bones is insufficient and the Yangming pulse is weak, dental diseases will arise.[17p]
    How can this be explained? The Yangming channel is associated with the metal element, while the teeth belong to the water element of the kidneys. The branches of Yangming enter the teeth, which serves as the mother's qi nourishing and protecting its offspring. Therefore, when Yangming is strong, the teeth are firm and strong; when it is weak, the teeth become loose.

    Hence, tooth pain occurs when external pathogens such as wind, cold, dampness, or heat invade the Yangming channel, accumulating and clashing with the qi and blood in the teeth, causing pain. If this heat and phlegm is abundant, there will be swelling and pain; if heat is not overly abundant, the gums may be slightly swollen and the roots feel elevated.

    Toothaches caused by cavities are due to damp-heat leading to decay, eroding the roots and causing pain. If there is bleeding between the teeth, this is because the branches of Yangming have allowed wind-heat pathogens to enter the gums, clashing with the blood, resulting in bleeding.

    Cavities occur when the Yangming channel is invaded by wind-heat pathogens, which clash with the qi and blood of the gums, leading to decay and the formation of purulent, foul-smelling fluid, referred to as tooth decay, or called "wind decay." Teeth that have (hidden worms) are those where worms have eroded the teeth down to the gums, resulting in pus and foul fluid.[18p]
    If there are protruding teeth, it is due to heat in the qi that transfers to the pulse, reaching the area between the teeth and gums, causing liquid foam to become pus; when qi and blood are exhausted, the flesh of the gums decays, resulting in exposed and protruding tooth roots. If the teeth are loose, it is due to the deficiency of the Yangming pulse, where qi and blood do not nourish, hence the looseness. If the teeth are darkened, it is because the marrow's qi and blood cannot flourish, leading to darkened teeth, referred to as "decayed teeth." The same applies to yellow and black teeth. From this, can we not say that all dental diseases arise from the Yangming? Liu Zonghou states: external invasion of wind and cold, or intake of cold through the mouth, causing tooth pain, are all external factors. Actual heat and false fire, bone steaming and qi stagnation, blood heat with insect damage, are all internal causes. Damage from hard objects is neither an internal nor external cause.

    In winter, when wind, cold, and dampness cause headaches, stiffness in the neck, and painful, loose teeth, one should take Mahuang powder. When severe cold attacks the brain, leading to both headaches and toothaches, one should take Xixin powder, Baizhi powder, or Scorpion Tail powder.[19p]
    To alleviate toothache, if using cooling medicines worsens the pain, one should treat it with a mixture of cardamom, Sichuan pepper, mint, schisandra, asarum, camphor, and fine salt ground to powder, applying it to the teeth. For pain that becomes worse with heat and subsides with cooling, treat with spicy and cooling medicines. If taking tonics for stomach heat leads to intolerable pain in upper and lower teeth, which pulls at the head causing intense pain, this is due to heat from the Yangming channel entering the brain. The patient prefers cold and despises heat, indicating heat in the Yangming channel. For teeth that prefer cold and dislike heat, use Qingwei Decoction.

    If there is more cold than heat, the patient mildly dislikes warm drinks and severely dislikes cold drinks, suggesting the use of cardamom powder. If there is more heat than cold, the patient mildly dislikes cold drinks and severely dislikes warm drinks; use musk powder or rapid effect powder. For upper teeth pain, use Shenma powder; for lower teeth pain, use Baizhi powder.

    Those who have habitually consumed a lot of meat may experience bad breath and loose, wobbly teeth, or constant bleeding, indicating internal injury from damp heat and excessive rich food, and should use Shenkong pill, Laoya powder, or a digestive powder with yellow medicine added. If heat causes tooth pain with swelling that spreads to the cheeks and jaw, this indicates heat in the Yangming channel, and one should use Jinfecao powder with ma huang and mint added as needed.[20p]
    Bone Socket Wind

    Someone asked: If the gums are swollen and painful, with intense cold and heat, and there is persistent decay, and treatments for dysentery are ineffective, what should be done? The response: This is known as Bone Socket Wind, also called Cheek Poison, caused by worries, thoughts, fright, and sorrow. It initially arises beneath the ear and between the neck, faintly under the skin, with a small nodule that gradually enlarges to the size of a walnut, becoming red and swollen, either above or below, or left or right, with a tight jaw making it impossible to eat. Begin by using a goose feather to probe and expel wind-phlegm. Take a Huanglian Detox Soup, along with Huangkui, Jiegeng, Chaihu, and Huangqin. Do not use knives or needles.

    Upper Palate Abscess

    Someone asked: If there is an ulcer on the upper palate, resembling a purple grape, what should be done? The response: This is called a Hanging Abscess, related to the Hand Taiyin and Hand Jueyin Pericardium, causing intense cold and heat, with the tongue unable to extend and the mouth unable to open and close, leading to a desire to lie on one’s back, with red discharge from the nose. This is due to heat accumulation in the Hand and Foot Shaoyin channels and the Sanjiao. It is advisable to use Huanglian Disinfecting Drink with added Jiegeng and Yuan Shen; urgently puncture to expel bad blood, and apply a Rhinoceros Horn and Amber ointment. For the robust, take a gold pill. If treatment is delayed, and food and drink cannot be taken, along with confused spirit and chaotic pulse, it can result in death.[21p]
    Tooth Abscess

    Someone asked: What about an abscess at the tooth root? It is called "attached tooth abscess," caused by heat and poison in the Yangming Stomach channel. It is advisable to use Qingwei San (Clear Stomach Powder) or Huanglian Jiaodu Decoction to detoxify, or to puncture and drain the bad blood for recovery.
    — From "Surgical Authenticity" by Chen Shigong (Ming Dynasty)

    Dental Disease

    Dental diseases can be caused by wind and fire, as well as damp-heat of the Yangming channel. Wind-related pain manifests with swelling upon exposure to wind, followed by pain, which can be treated with the Dispelling Wind Powder. Fire-related pain involves the tooth root pulling at the jaw and cheek, producing intermittent sharp pain, which can be alleviated by applying Ice Boron Powder, allowing saliva to flow and resolve the issue. When damp-heat in the Yangming channel causes pain, the affected areas may swell; in severe cases, this can pull at the temples, causing pain in the neck, with heat in the mouth and constipation. It would be appropriate to use Liangge San (Cool the Diaphragm Powder) with gypsum for treatment. If the swelling is high and soft, there is likely pus inside that should be lanced with a needle for drainage and healing. For gingival diseases that bleed incessantly, internally take Rhinoceros Horn and Rehmannia Decoction, and externally apply Ren Zhong Bai Powder. In children with teething issues, if the tooth root pierces the gum, causing pain like a thorn in the lip, use a beryllium needle to puncture the gum, removing the original tooth with the hand. If bleeding does not stop, replace with damp paper multiple times until the bleeding ceases. It is essential to avoid rich flavors, and the teeth will regrow as before.[22p]
    Zouma Gan

    Zouma Gan refers to a condition that develops rapidly and cannot be delayed in treatment. This ailment often arises from residual toxins of measles or smallpox, and can also be exacerbated by other severe illnesses. The condition manifests with decayed roots of teeth, resulting in a foul and blackened state. In severe cases, the gums may recede, and the roots become black and rotten, leading to the tearing of the cheeks and lips within a few days, which is indeed incurable.

    At the initial onset, it is advisable to use aloe vera for a decoction to treat the condition, and externally apply either Ren Zhong Bai powder or Bing Peng powder to the affected area. The goal is to remove the blackened decay; the presence of fresh red flesh and bleeding is a good sign. If, at the time of treatment, the rotten flesh does not detach, and the decay begins to widen, along with continued swelling and persistent foul odor, and accompanied by unresolved body heat, these are all indications of an incurable condition.[23p]
    On Teeth

    The "Suwen" states: For men, at the age of eight, the kidney energy is strong, and teeth begin to regenerate. At the age of thirty-eight, true teeth emerge; at fifty-eight, the teeth become worn; and by eighty-eight, the teeth are gone. The same applies to women, with seven being the corresponding number. The kidneys govern the bones, and teeth are the markers of bone, nourished by the marrow. All teeth belong to the kidneys, while the upper and lower gums belong to Yangming. The upper gums prefer cold and dislike heat; they relate to the foot Yangming stomach. The lower gums prefer heat and dislike cold; they relate to the hand Yangming large intestine. Any looseness, exposure or pain—whether painful or not, with or without bleeding—all presenting as if about to fall, are associated with the kidneys. The classic states: the heat of the kidneys leads to a black complexion and worn teeth. It also states: when the lesser yin is in decline, the face appears black, teeth extend and become coated. Conditions such as dental caries with swollen, immobile, ulcerating, foul-smelling gums all belong to Yangming. When there are complications from mixed influences or external causes, treatment should differentiate between deficiency and excess.[24p]
    In cases of kidney deficiency and cold, use Anshen Pills or Huanshao Dan; if severe, use the Bawei Pills to address it. During the cold winter months, if severe cold invades the head causing headaches and pain in the teeth and gums, this indicates an invasion of cold affecting both the Greater Yang and Lesser Yin. Zhongjing used the Mahuang, Fuzi, and Xixin Decoction for those with kidney deficiency, which is often present. If there is tooth pain, looseness, fatigue in the limbs, and a lack of appetite, this points to a deficiency in both the spleen and kidney; in such cases, Anshen Pills and Buzhong Yiqi Decoction should be taken together.

    If someone prefers cold and dislikes heat, this indicates injury to the blood of the stomach; use the Qingwei Decoction. If they dislike cold but favor heat, this suggests injury to the stomach qi; use the Buzhong Yiqi Decoction. Whenever tooth pain is triggered by exertion, particularly more so in the afternoon, or accompanied by thirst and a dark complexion, or nocturnal emissions, these all indicate heat from spleen and kidney deficiency; for this, use the Buzhong Yiqi along with Liuwuwei Pills or the Shiquan Dabu Decoction. If there is swelling and pain in the gums along with swelling of the cheeks, this indicates wind-heat in the stomach channel; use the Xijiao Shengma Decoction. If one drinks a lot and experiences tooth pain with cheek swelling, this indicates damp-heat in the stomach channel; use the Qingwei Decoction with Gegen, or a Jiexin Decoction.[25p]
    Discussion on Dental Diseases

    For toothache caused by kidney deficiency, the remedy is the Ziyin Dabu Pill combined with deer antler. The kidneys govern the bones; when the kidneys are deficient, the marrow weakens. Weak marrow leads to brittle bones, and brittle bones cannot hold the teeth securely, resulting in loose teeth. This can be compared to a broken table: if the wood is weak, the joints become loose and the wood can easily shake out. However, when it is nourished by water, the table is restored and the joints become secure. Thus, the treatment here focuses on nourishing the yin and replenishing the kidneys. When the kidneys are not deficient, the gums and bones are moist, and when the gums and bones are moist, the teeth are secure. This formula includes cooked rehmannia, achyranthes, eucommia, cornelian cherry, five-flavor fruit, and goji berries, all of which are substances that promote yin and benefit the kidneys.[26p]
    Ba JI, conrong, fennel, yuanzhi, shichangpu, yam, and Fuling are all sweet and warm items. They can warm the kidneys and generate essence. As for deer antler, it is sourced from blood and qi, and possesses the most complete yin energy, hence it is used as a supplement to nourish the kidneys and replenish essence and marrow. The flesh of red dates is sweet and benefits the spleen, thus it is used in pill formulations.

    When the Grand Minister of Qi had a toothache, Cang Gong made him a bitter angelica stew, which he gargled with three sheng daily; after five or six days, the illness was resolved. The bitterness soothes the tooth pests, and its coldness dispels wind and heat. Later generations, lacking tooth pests, still used bitter angelica for dental hygiene; prolonged use could lead to lower back issues, due to excess. This shows a lack of understanding regarding the affairs of the military and the politics of military actions, as none have succeeded without knowing these aspects.

    For toothaches that are aggravated by cold and relieved by heat, the "Tooth Powder" is the remedy. When a person sleeps and opens their mouth, wind and cold can enter, leading to toothaches; consuming cold drinks exacerbates the affliction, while warm drinks dispel the cold and provide some relief. This formula contains Aconite and Chuanwu, both pungent and warming ingredients, used to warm away the cold.[27p]
    The whole scorpion is a slightly toxic substance; it can be used to counteract cold poison and treat wind evils. Some prepare a decoction with dried ginger, black cardamom, and asarum to rinse with, which also serves to address cold issues.

    For toothaches caused by wind-heat, which prefer cold and dislike heat, one should use Dingfeng Decoction for rinsing. This is due to the internal presence of wind-heat affecting the cheeks, where the邪火 becomes strong, leading to tooth pain. Therefore, consuming cold drinks can mildly balance yin and yang, alleviating pain, while hot drinks may exacerbate the fire and intensify the pain.

    In this formula, we use tooth soap, schizonepeta, and green onion for their acrid warmth to disperse wind, and saltpeter and gypsum for their salty cold properties to drive off the heat.

    For tooth pain associated with holes between the teeth, a combination of five ingredients—wutong tears, toad venom, thorn apple seeds, leek seeds, and lime—used in any one of these will yield remarkable results.[28p]
    The phoenix tree weeps, indicating the toxicity of fire and wind diseases (with pests hidden beneath). Wang Hai often found this remarkable; toad venom leads to dental erosion, causing pain everywhere, which Lin Yuanli often found remarkable; the seeds of the wild tobacco cause vapor to expel pests (hiding beneath), which Master Sun often found remarkable; leeks burned with mugwort create smoke that drives away pests (hiding beneath), which Zhu Danxi often found remarkable. These are all methods of ancient times.

    Now, I have obtained a new prescription: it involves simply using newly burned lime and honey pills applied directly to the areas of dental erosion, which will heal promptly—this has not been discussed by the ancients. The "Benshi Fang" states: To extract a tooth without touching the hand, take equal amounts of black cohosh and spikenard, and double the amount of Sichuan pepper and asarum, ground finely. Use a small amount on a needle to rub inside and outside the affected tooth several times; thus, if the tooth is daily injured, it will easily fall out. All four ingredients are spicy and hot; if applied repeatedly to the gums, they will gradually separate, which is a principle-based method.[29p]
    The Complete Book of Jingyue
    [Ming Dynasty - Zhang Jiebin]

    On Evidence

    There are three types of dental diseases: the first is fire, the second is wind, and the third is kidney deficiency. Each of these diseases has different treatments; once the true nature is discerned, it is not difficult to treat dental issues.

    For those with fire-related diseases, the pain must be located in the muscles around the gums, which may manifest as swelling, pain, erosion, foul odor, or bleeding from the gaps between teeth. All these symptoms indicate a problem within the meridians. The upper teeth are associated with the foot yangming channel and remain still; whereas, the lower teeth are associated with the hand yangming channel and move continuously when chewing. This illness is likely caused by an excess of rich foods, fine wines, and sweet flavors, leading to damp heat accumulating in the intestines and stomach, which then obstructs the meridians. Therefore, the treatment should focus on avoiding lavish foods and clearing the fire pathogen.[30p]
    For those suffering from dental diseases, the issue lies not in the meridians but in the teeth, mainly caused by damp heat transforming into tooth worms, which leads to erosion and cavities, resulting in decayed and painful teeth. The treatment should primarily focus on eliminating the worms. For those with strong damp heat, it is also advisable to clear the stomach fire.

    In cases where dental issues arise from kidney deficiency, the problem lies not in the meridians but in the organs, as teeth are the endpoints of bones, and bones are governed by the kidneys. Hence, it is said that when the kidneys weaken, the teeth loosen; when essence is firm, the teeth are strong. When there is a dental ailment, it manifests as brittle and weak teeth, which may be loose, spaced, or protruding and hollow. Any dental disease not caused by worms or fire is surely due to insufficient kidney energy, which may result from a congenital deficiency or postnatal depletion, both of which can lead to this condition. Therefore, the treatment should primarily focus on specifically nourishing kidney energy.

    Injuries due to external factors, whether from impact, falls, or excessive biting into hard objects, will eventually lead to tooth damage; this cannot be cured by medicine. The wise should take precautions themselves![31p]
    Treatment Methods

    For toothache caused by yangming heat and obstruction, it is advisable to use formulas like Qingwei San or Qingwei Yin. If the fire is severe, one should use Chaoxin Yin or Taiqing Yin to clear its source. If there is a deficiency of kidney yin, and stomach fire is excessive, leading to thirst and swelling, Yu Nv Jian is the best remedy.

    For treating tooth pain externally, only warm and pungent herbs can disperse the heat; recommended are formulas like Xixin Jian, Dingxiang San, Jianghuang San, and Fuyan San. Among these, Erxin Jian and Sanxiang San are particularly effective.

    For pain from cavities caused by dental caries, one should use formulas like the Leek Seed Decoction from the Ruizhutang, Ba Dou Wan, or Lilu San, any of which can be chosen for use.

    Continuous bleeding from the gums is caused by stomach fire and should be treated with medications that clear the stomach.[32p]
    There is also a deficiency in yin below and a blocking of yang above; thus, the six pulses are weak and fine, completely not representing an excess of heat. If blood from the gums flows profusely and cannot be stopped, and if the hands and feet are cold, one should promptly use a calming yin decoction to address this; if one carelessly uses cold and cooling methods, it will surely lead to doom.

    For kidney deficiency causing teeth to be unstable—either shaking or brittle and protruding—it is advisable to focus on tonifying the kidneys, but one must also differentiate between cold and heat conditions. Generally, formulations like Left Kidney Pill and Six Flavor Pill strengthen the yin of the kidneys, while Right Kidney Pill and Eight Flavor Pill can tonify the yang of the kidneys; adding bone fragment supplement is particularly effective in pill form. If the teeth are loose or falling out, or if there is bleeding from the gums without foul smell or pain, this indicates yin's yang deficiency; thus, it is suitable to use calming kidney pills or similar remedies.

    "Running Horse Tooth Decay" describes the condition where the gums decay and the teeth fall out, indicating urgency. This is due to the accumulation of heat toxicity. Anyone suffering from this condition faces significant danger. Upon initial appearance of these symptoms, one should swiftly drain the yangming heat and regularly consume mung bean drink. Externally, use Ice White Powder, Ice Jade Powder, Three Immortals Powder, Musk and Alumen Powder, and Northern Jujube Dan for application.[33p]
    Secret Manual of the Stone Chamber
    [Qing Dynasty, Chen Shiduo]

    Life-Extending Teeth

    The method for long teeth: First, use a complete set of the spine of a male rat, discarding the remaining bones and the tail. One part of musk and dried cooked root of prepared Rehmannia must be used. Crush and fry the remaining bones, and make a fine powder, each amounting to three qian. The prepared Rehmannia must be made by oneself and must not come into contact with iron utensils, for if it does, all the previous ingredients will be ineffective. Fresh Rehmannia must also be inspected; if it has been pierced with an iron needle, it will also be ineffective. Three parts of asarum and three parts of elm bark. In summary, all the herbs must not come into contact with iron utensils. One qian of angelica, two qian of green salt, and one qian of eucommia is sufficient, all ground into a very fine powder. The rat bones should be cleaned of flesh and dried on a new tile, ground into powder without burning, in order to retain their natural essence. Place it in a ceramic bottle and at the fifth watch each day, ensure no sound is made. Lightly rub this medicine on the toothless areas thirty-six times, allowing it to naturally be swallowed without rinsing the mouth with water, and continue this for a month. Rubbing during midday is even better, following the same method as before.[34p]
    Firm Teeth

    Prescription for Firm Teeth: Use a set of male rat vertebrae, along with three qian each of cooked rehmannia, asarum, elm bark, and fragmented bones, one qian each of blue salt and angelica, and two qian of eucommia. Grind them into powder, wrap in cotton paper into strips, and bite on the gums until the flavor is exhausted; this will prevent teeth from falling out forever. However, it should not come into contact with iron utensils, as it will be ineffective. This medicine can benefit hundreds of people. Generally, one person needs three strips.

    Grind these together, make a paste, and decoct in water to take.

    Killing虫 Pills

    For treating toothache caused by worms.

    Take a good amount of arsenic (without being too strict on the quantity) and a little bit of yellow lead. Melt them together with yellow wax to form a lump. Then, roll it into pills about the size of a soybean, wrap them in white cotton, leaving a tail.

    If the right tooth aches, insert it into the right ear; if the left tooth aches, insert it into the left ear; if both sides hurt, insert them into both ears, making sure they go deep into the ear canal. By the end of the night, the worms will die, and the pain shall never return.

    Crying and Smiling Powder

    For rapidly treating tooth pain effectively.

    Ingredients: Realgar, myrrh, pepper, musk, nutmeg, ginger, fine cinnamon—grind these equally into a powder. Use a little bit and blow it into the left nostril for men and the right nostril for women. The pain will immediately stop.

    If headache and eyelid swelling occur, roll the powdered medicine into a strip, dip it in fragrant oil, light it, and burn it on the painful tooth area. Once the strip is burned out, the pain will instantly cease.

    Toothache Recipe

    Ingredients: Realgar, myrrh each one qian, fine cinnamon five fen. Grind these into a powder; if the left side hurts, use a little bit and insert it into the left nostril, then blow into the right ear; if the right side hurts, use it in the right nostril and blow into the left ear.

    Chive Seed Pills

    For treating toothache caused by worms.

      Method for Extracting Painful Teeth

    Take 1 liang of Sichuan pepper and xixin; 5 qian each of草乌 (plant) and荜茇 (spice). Grind the above into a fine powder, and apply a small amount to the painful tooth so it falls out.

    Method for Cavities

    Take 1 qian of borax and vermilion; 2 qian of nitre; 7 pieces of pointed Sichuan black nightshade; 14 pieces of aconite; 7 pieces of toad venom; 2 qian of arsenic. On May 5th, grind into powder, take a small amount to apply onto the teeth. After the tooth falls out, use防风 (plant),荆芥 (plant), and甘草 (licorice) to make a decoction for rinsing the mouth.

    Method for Regrowth of Teeth

    One male mouse, skinned, rubbed with nitre for three days until the flesh decays completely. Take the bones and dry them on a tile. Then take 1 liang of香附 (plant), and 3 qian each of白芷 (plant),川芎 (plant),桑白皮 (plant),地骨皮 (plant),蒲公英 (dandelion),川椒 (Sichuan pepper),旱莲草 (plant),明净青盐 (clear blue salt), and川槿皮 (plant). Grind into a fine powder, rub for 100 days, and the teeth will regrow—this is a good method.

    Another Method

    Three or four soft, unweaned mice; 5 qian each of白芨 (plant),白芷 (plant),青盐 (blue salt),细辛 (xixin),当归 (dong quai), and熟地黄 (reheating processed Chinese yam). First, grind the five ingredients into a powder, then mix with Chinese yam until it becomes paste-like, form into a cake, wrap the mice inside, and cover with wet paper. Burn with gentle and strong fire until the smoke is gone. Remove and grind into powder, apply to the area to promote tooth growth.

    Xie Fu's Remedy for Tooth Pain

    Tooth Strengthening Powder

    Used for unbearable tooth pain in the upper and lower jaws caused by the intake of stomach-warming medicines, leading to pulling in the head and a hot, painful face. Choose coptis in three parts; if it’s not good, increase it by two parts. Double the amount in summer.     Tooth Gate

    Formulation

    Musk, Realgar, and Cinnabar Powder: Used for treating adults and children's loose teeth, exposed gums, bone socket wind toxins, erosion, and decay, preventing them from eating. Ingredients: Musk, Dragon Bone, Realgar, and Cinnabar.

    First, grind each to a fine powder, using a goose feather dipped in the medicine to apply to the affected area. Additionally, take three qian (a traditional weight unit) mixed with seven parts water, boil down to five parts, then take a warm sip to hold in the mouth before spitting out; alternatively, wash the teeth daily with warm water.

    Cooked Copper Powder: Used for teeth that fall out at inappropriate times, making them secure. Ingredients: 2.5 qian each of Angelica sinensis, Asarum, and Earth Skin, plus one liang of cooked copper powder.

    Grind these to a fine powder and apply to the affected area, sealing with wax paper. Do this two to three times a day for three to five days to achieve stability; avoid chewing hard substances.

    Honeycomb Powder: Used for teeth that do not grow and for toothache due to wind.[42p]
    Beehive dew, cleared of thorn, pepper to remove eyes and mouth, stir-fried until sweating; earth bone skin, pine resin, blue salt, and white alum, each one tael. Grind these into a fine powder. Each time, use five fen, wrap it in cotton and apply to the affected area, chew it, and spit out the saliva.

    Chuan Shengma powder treats the failure of teeth to grow and tooth wind exposing. Chuan Shengma and Bai Fuzhi, each one tael. Grind these into a fine powder and mix well. In August, take four jin of fresh dandelion, wash off the soil, squeeze to obtain two large cups of juice, mix with the powder, and place it in a magnetic vessel. Each time, use a willow twig wrapped in cotton, dip one end in the medicine, heat it until hot, and apply to the seams under the roots of the teeth, then coat with a little paste for immediate effect.

    For swollen and bleeding gums: one and a half qian of realgar, one character of musk, copper green, light powder, yellow vine, and calcined yellow lead, each one qian; blood resin and white alum, each five fen. Grind these into a fine powder, mix well, and apply a little to the affected area.

    Huanglian powder treats bleeding between the gums, preventing eating. Huanglian, white dragon bone, and horse's tooth nitrate, each one tael; white alum five fen; and dragon's brain one qian. Grind these into a fine powder, and each time, apply a little to the roots of the teeth.

    Shengji Taohua powder treats bleeding from the gums and sometimes bleeding from openings. Calcinated cold water stone, three qian; flying cinnabar, one qian; stir-fried licorice, one character; half a character of prussic acid. Grind these into a fine powder and mix well, applying a little to the affected area.[43p]
    Yujin Powder - Treats bleeding gums.
    Ingredients: Equal parts of Yujin, Baizhi, and Xixin.
    Grind to a fine powder, use to brush teeth. Additionally, boil bamboo leaves and bamboo skin, add a little salt, and can also be used for rinsing.

    Hemorrhage from Gums Formula
    Ingredients: 2 qian of calcined alum, 5 fen of乳香, a small amount of musk.
    Grind to a fine powder, gently rub on the gums for a long time, and rinse with saline.

    Divine Effect Powder - Treats bleeding between teeth.
    Ingredients: Equal parts of Caowu, Qingyan, and Zaojia.
    Place in a ceramic vessel, burn to ash, and when using, apply a small amount to teeth for immediate effect.

    Toothache Formula for Kidney Deficiency and Stomach Heat
    Ingredients: 4 liang of mutton bone ash, 5 liang of gypsum, 1 qian of Huanglian, 5 qian each of Shengmā, Shengdihuang, and 3 qian of Wutong tears, 5 fen of Longdancao.
    Grind to a powder, use to brush teeth and rinse with water.

    Yuchi Powder - Treats toothache from wind and worms, loose and decayed teeth; or it may turn into bone socket wind with pus and blood.
    Ingredients: 1 qian each of Diguopi, Baizhi, Xixin, Fangfeng, Shengma, Chuanxiong, Danggui, Huaihua, Gaoben, and licorice.
    Grind into a paste, add 3 slices of fresh ginger and 100 black beans, boil hot and use as a mouthwash, spitting out when cooled.

    Jingjiao Decoction - Treats tooth pain from wind and heat.
    Ingredients: 3 qian each of Jingjiao, Mint, Shengma, and Xixin.[44p]
    The above text provides various traditional remedies for toothache and related conditions.

    1. For toothache due to wind and cold:
      Grind the following into a powder: Bai Zhi, Xi Xin, Liang Jiang, Bi Ba, Chuan Jiao, Xiang Fu Zi, and Bee Honeycomb, each in equal parts. Use three qian (a measure) with water to decoct and gargle, or apply it.

    2. Pepper and Salt Powder:
      For pain from cavities: Grind together one qian each of Chuan Jiao, white salt, and Bee Honeycomb. Mix with three stalks of green onion, decoct in water, and use hot for gargling and cold for spitting out.

    3. Beecomb Powder (from "Hui Chun"):
      For pain from wind and cavities, which is unbearable. Grind the ingredients and decoct in a mixture of water and vinegar for hot gargling and cold spitting out.

    4. Ten Whole and Greatly Supplementing Decoction:
      For painful hollow teeth: Use one qian each of Ren Shen, Bai Zhu (stir-fried), Bai Shao (stir-fried), peeled Bai Fu Ling, processed Huang Qi, Dang Gui, processed Gan Cao, Shu Di, and Chuan Xiong, with two fen of Gui Xin. Add two slices of ginger and three jujubes, then decoct for consumption.

    5. Ma Huang, Fu Zi, and Xi Xin Decoction (from Zhongjing):
      For yang deficiency toothaches: Use two liang each of Ma Huang (cut into sections) and Xi Xin (cleaned), and one piece of Fu Zi. Decoct with water for consumption.

    6. Ge Hua Jie Cheng Decoction:
      For toothache caused by excessive drinking: Combine five fen each of Ge Hua, Sha Ren, Bai Dou Kou, Chen Pi, Ren Shen, and Bai Fu Ling, and two fen each of Shen Qu (stir-fried), Bai Zhu (stir-fried), Gan Jiang, and Qing Pi (peeled and stir-fried), along with Ze Xie. Decoct for consumption.[45p]
      Heavenly South Star Pill treats phlegm and fire rising causing toothache.

    Powder heavenly south star, sulfur, gypsum, nitrate, all in equal parts. Grind to a fine powder, mix with flour to form pills the size of a Chinese parasol seed. Take twenty pills each time on an empty stomach, at noon, and before bed.

    Rhino Horn and Rehmannia Decoction treats yin deficiency and excessive fire causing toothache.

    Use two and a half qian of powdered rhino horn, peony root; two qian of white peony; and one and a half liang of raw rehmannia. Boil in water and take.

    Cool the Stomach Powder treats stomach fire causing swollen and painful gums, and tooth sensitivity.

    Use one liang each of yellow qin wine fried, gardenia fried, and mint; four liang of forsythia; and two liang each of rhubarb, sodium sulfate, and licorice, soaked in yellow wine. Grind into a powder, take five qian each time.

    Dispersing Wind Powder treats wind and fire toothache.

    Use the spikes of schizopepon, prepared licorice, dried tangerine peel, thick pericarp fried in ginger juice, patchouli, cicada molting, ginseng, fried silkworms, poria, saposhnikovia, and qianghuo. Boil in water and take.

    Castor Bean Pill, also known as One Smile Powder, treats tooth pain from cavities.

    Take one castor bean and fifty grains of Sichuan pepper, ground finely. Make into a very fine powder, form into pills the size of millet, and stuff into cavities.

    Alismatis Powder treats insect-induced tooth pain.

    Use an unspecified amount of alisma, grind to powder and stuff into the cavity, avoiding swallowing any juice; expectorate saliva. It has remarkable efficacy.[46p]
    Leek Seed Soup: Treats worm-eaten teeth.
    Take a pinch of leek seeds. Place in a bowl, burn to create smoke, and using a small bamboo tube split at the bottom into four openings, cover the opening with paper shaped like a trumpet to guide the smoke to the decayed tooth. If it’s a lower tooth, rinse with a concentrated decoction of the seeds; the worms will come out by themselves.

    North Jujube Decoction: Treats rampant tooth decay.
    Take one pitted North jujube, insert a weight of arsenic into the jujube and heat to keep it intact, grind finely, and apply a small amount to the affected area.

    Three Immortals Powder: Treats rampant tooth decay which can cause immediate death if it rots.
    Three parts of verdigris, one part of musk, and one piece of white sediment from a woman’s urine bucket, calcined, about four grams in total. Grind to a very fine powder and apply, but do not use too much.

    Rhinoceros Horn and Cimicifuga Decoction: Treats wind-heat toothache.
    Seven grams of powdered rhinoceros horn, five and a half grams each of ledebouriella and notopterygium, two and a half grams each of angelica, scutellaria, and white peony, and one and a half grams of licorice, along with five grams of cimicifuga. Decoct seven grams in water for each dosage.

    Amber and Rhinoceros Horn Ointment: Treats fiery tooth pain and elevated dental sensitivity.
    Finely grind real amber and fresh rhinoceros horn shavings, each one gram. Remove the husk from ginseng, pit from sour jujube seeds, and peel from poria, and grind together, each two grams. Grind the plates of brain powder finely. Mix these into a fine powder evenly, then refine with honey to form an ointment and store in a ceramic container. When symptoms arise, take a piece the size of a bullet, dissolve in a concentrated decoction of lily bulbs, and take five doses in one day.[47p]
    Jia Jian Gan Lu Yin (Sweet Dew Decoction)
    This is used to treat stomach heat and toothaches.
    Ingredients:

    • 1 ounce of cooked Rehmannia
    • 1 ounce of raw Rehmannia
    • 1 ounce of Asparagus (remove the heart)
    • 1 ounce of Scutellaria
    • 1 ounce of Bitter Orange Peel
    • 1 ounce of Loquat Leaf (remove hairs)
    • 1 ounce of Artemisia
    • 1 ounce of Dendrobium
    • 0.5 ounces of Licorice
    • 0.5 ounces of Rhinoceros Horn
      Grind these into a powder. For each dose, take 0.6 ounces, mix with a cup of water, and boil until reduced by a third. Strain and take warm after meals or before lying down. For children, divide the dose into two and adjust accordingly.

    She Fan San (Musk and Alum Powder)
    Used to treat rampant toothache and severe symptoms.
    Ingredients:

    • A small amount of Musk
    • 0.5 ounces of Alum
    • 0.25 ounces of Verdigris
    • 0.1 ounces of raw Alumen
      Grind the above into a fine powder and apply to the affected tooth area.

      Huanglian Xiaodu San - Treats real heat tooth pain.

    Buzhong Yiqi Tang - Treats qi deficiency tooth pain.

    Gui Pi Decoction: Used for blood not returning to the channels, presenting with dental bleeding.

    Liu Wei Wan: Used for deficiency of water and excess fire causing toothache.

    Ingredients: 8 liang of Shou Di, steamed with wine; 4 liang each of Shan Yu Rou and Fu Ling mixed with milk; 3 liang each of Shan Yao, Ze Xie, and Mu Dan Pi; 1 liang each of Fu Zi and Rou Gui. Make into pills the size of a tung seed, and take with salty warm water.

    Ba Wei Wan: Used for deficiency fire in the Ming Men (Gate of Life) leading to toothache.

    Ingredients: 8 liang of Shou Di mixed with sand and steamed nine times; 4 liang each of Shan Yu Rou and Shan Yao moistened with wine; 3 liang each of Fu Ling mixed with milk, Dan Pi, and Ze Xie; 1 liang each of Fu Zi and Rou Gui.

    Yin Chen San: Used for toothache, with external redness, swelling, and wind-heat in the bone sockets.

    Ingredients: 2.5 qians each of Yin Chen, Lian Qiao, Ban Xia, Jing Jie Sui, Ma Huang, Sheng Ma, Huang Qin, Mu Dan Pi, She Gan, Qiang Huo, Du Huo, Da Huang Pao, Bo He, and Jiang Can; 5 qians of Xi Xin; 1 liang of Qian Niu. Grind into a fine powder, taking 3 qian each time. Boil one cup of water, then add the powdered medicine, stir well, and take urgently after meals along with the dregs while hot.[50p]
    Qianghuo Fuzitang (Qianghuo and Aconite Decoction) 【Dongyuan】
    Treats severe cold in winter, affecting the brain, causing pain in the head and teeth, referred to as "brain wind." This condition can be very harmful and requires this remedy.

    • Ephedra (dried, without sections), Aconite (processed), each 3 grams
    • Qianghuo (Notopterygium), Cangzhu (Atractylodes), each 5 grams
    • Huangqi (Astragalus) 1 gram
    • Fangfeng (Siler), Gancao (Licorice), Shengma (Cimicifuga), Baijiangcan (fried, silk removed), Huanglian (Coptis), Baizhi (Angelica), each 3 grams
    • Fouer grass is used if there is a cold cough; if not, do not use.
      Boil with water and take.

    Duhuo San (Duhuo Powder)

    • Jingjie (Schizonepeta), Bohe (Peppermint), Sheng Dihuang (Fresh Rehmannia), Xixin (Asarum).

    • Danggui (Angelica sinensis), Shudi (Rehmannia), each 6 grams.

    Dong Gui Long Dan Powder: Treats cold-heat toothache.

    Yi Zhi Mu Lu Powder: Treats cold-heat tooth pain.
    Ingredients: Cao Dou Kou (2.2 qian), Yi Zhi Ren, Dong Gui Body, Shu Di Huang, Yang Jing Guo Ash (0.5 qian each), Mu Lu (0.2 qian), Sheng Ma (1.5 qian), Huang Lian (0.4 qian). Grind into fine powder for application. If there is cold tooth pain, omit Mu Lu.

    Cao Dou Kou Powder (Dan Xi): Treats tooth pain with more cold and less heat.
    Ingredients: Cao Dou Kou (1.2 qian), Huang Lian (2.5 qian), Sheng Ma (2.5 qian), Xi Xin Ye and Fang Feng (0.2 qian each), Dong Gui Body (0.6 qian), Shu Di Huang, Yang Jing Guo Ash (0.5 qian each). Grind into fine powder and apply to the painful area.[53p]
    Musk Powder: Treats conditions with more heat and less cold; symptoms include gums and teeth becoming loose, bleeding, teeth moving as if they might fall out, intense pain, and difficulty eating. Ingredients: 1.5 qian of Schizonepeta, 1.5 qian of Coptis, 1.5 qian of Amomum, 1 fen of Rehmannia, 1 fen of Ephedra, 2.5 fen of Alpinia, a small amount of musk, and 2 qian of ash from sheep's hoof fat, along with 3 fen each of ginseng, fresh Rehmannia, and Angelica, prepared with Han Fangji wine. Grind into a fine powder and use a small amount to rub on the painful tooth area, holding it for a long time until saliva is produced and expelled.

    Immediate Effect Powder (from Dongyuan): Treats unbearable tooth pain as well as pain in the head, neck, and back. Symptoms include slight aversion to cold drinks and severe aversion to hot drinks; the pulse shows yang deficiency and yin excess in all three regions, indicating internal excess in the five organs and deficiency in the yang pathways of the six fu organs, with a weak and fine pulse, and frequent, slippery urination. Ingredients: 1 qian of Siler, 3 fen of honey-fried Licorice, 4 fen of gentian washed in liquor, 7 fen of Schizonepeta, and 2 fen of Asarum. Boil with 1 cup of water until reduced to 5 fen, strain out dregs, and use a spoon to swish in the mouth over the painful area; relief is immediate. If there is a stronger aversion to hot drinks, add 1 qian of gentian; if pains worsen with wind, add 5 fen each of Amomum and Coptis, but do not add gentian. Adjust the ingredients as necessary based on the amount of heat and cold.[54p]
    Shengma Powder treats upper jaw tooth pain.
    Components: Increased Xi Xin, Huang Bo, Zhi Mu, Fang Ji, Huang Lian, Sheng Ma, Bai Zhi, Man Jing Zi, Niu Bang Zi, and Bo He. Grind these ingredients into a fine powder, mix with peppermint tea to take internally or apply to the gums; decoction is also acceptable.

    Bai Zhi Powder treats lower jaw tooth pain.
    Components: Bai Zhi, Fang Feng, Lian Qiao, calcined Shi Gao, Jing Jie, Chi Shao Yao, and increased Bo He. Grind these into a fine powder, mix with peppermint tea to take internally or apply to the gums; decoction is also acceptable.

    Shengong Pill (from Dong Yuan) treats swollen and painful gums. If Lan Xiang Ye is unavailable, replace it with Huo Xiang. Each of the following: Dang Gui, Mu Xiang (not exposed to fire) 1 qian, Sheng Ma 2 qian, Sheng Di Huang (washed with wine and baked), Sheng Gan Cao 3 qian each, Huang Lian (remove impurities and wash with wine), Su He Sha Ren 5 qian each. Grind these into a fine powder and make pills the size of a mung bean using a dough made from soup and steamed cakes. Take 100 pills each time, or increase to 200, with white soup when taken, and at a distance from meals. It also treats blood dysentery and hemorrhaging, continuous blood discharge, blood that is brown, purple, or black, and blood in the intestines. Take on an empty stomach with rice soup. For pulses that are surging and slow, it also treats numbness and qi rising, obstructed qi, and hallucinations.[55p]
    Lao Ya San (Loosened Tooth Powder)
    (From Dongyuan)

    It treats swollen and painful gums, loose teeth, teeth that do not grow, yellow teeth, and bad breath.

    Ingredients:

    • Shengma (Radix Cimicifugae)
    • Qianghuo (Notopterygium)
    • Sheep tibia ash, each one liang
    • Longdancao (Gentian) washed in wine, one liang and five qian

    Prepare the above as a fine powder. Use gauze to sieve the bone ash into a fine dust, then mix well and apply to the gums at night.

    Shengma in the ancient text is recorded as four fen, which is equivalent to one liang.

    Hei Xi Dan (Black Tin Pills)
    Treats severe toothache due to yang deficiency.

    Ingredients:

    • Black lead
    • Sulfur, each two liang.[56p]
      To the right, prepare to melt sulfur, gradually incorporating it until it forms into sheets. Wait for it to produce a toxic fire on the ground, and grind it until it makes no sound.

    Lao Ya San - for treating weak teeth that cannot chew food.

    Use three qian of Sheng Ma, one qian each of Sheng Di Huang, and Shi Gao; five qian each of Bai Fu Ling and Yuan Shen; three fen each of burned sheep tibia ash and Wutong tears; one qian and three fen of Huang Lian; a small amount of musk to be ground separately. The above ingredients should be ground into a fine powder and mixed well. Use a small amount to rub on the teeth before sleeping, and then rinse with warm water.

    Tou Guan San - for treating dental issues caused by cold wind.

    Use seven pieces each of centipede heads, the stingers of dried scorpions (to remove toxins), large as wheat grains of Chuan Wu, and thin as coins of Chuan Wu; seven grains of male yellow (realgar), ground separately; seven grains of pepper. Grind the above into a fine powder, use a paper twist to dip in vinegar, apply a small amount of the medicine on a fire to dry it, plug into both ears, and keep the mouth closed for a while; it works immediately.

    Shua Ya Lao Ya San - for eliminating wind-cold cavities and providing great efficacy.

    Use a little salt, ground finely; forty-nine branches each of four-inch-long locust and willow; seven stems of non-cavity soap pods. Combine these in a ceramic jar, seal with yellow clay, burn in husk fire overnight, wait for it to cool down, then grind finely for regular use.

    Bai Ya San - for treating yellow or black teeth.

    Use one qian each of Shi Gao and Sheng Ma; seven fen of Bai Zhi; a small amount of musk; two qian of sheep tibia ash. Grind the above into a fine powder and use warm water to rinse the mouth and apply it to the teeth effectively.[57p]
    Musk Tooth Powder strengthens teeth and whitens them. The formula includes 1 part musk, 10 grams of rhizoma ligustici chuanxiong, 20 grams of huanglian, 3.5 grams each of sheep bone ash, white cardamom, and grass cardamom, 3 parts of processed rehmannia and 2 parts of both raw and cooked rehmannia, three pieces of myrrh, one gallnut. Grind into a fine powder and use as before.

    Eternal Spring Tooth Powder prevents tooth wind and promotes dark hair. The ingredients are 50 grams each of chuanxiong, sand ginger, fragrant wood, decoction of various herbs, cloves, rhizoma ligustici chuanxiong, gallnut, poria, asarum, blue salt, alum, sweet wood, white tribulus, and sandalwood, as well as 200 grams of gypsum, nine pieces of myrrh, nine pieces of terminalia chebula fruit, 30 grams of copper sulfate, and 5 grams of musk. Grind into a fine powder, mix well, and brush teeth morning and evening, followed by rinsing with warm water and spitting out.

    Agarwood Powder strengthens teeth and nourishes hair. The ingredients are 20 grams each of agarwood, terminalia chebula peel, blue salt, and indigo, 15 grams each of white sandalwood and mother clove, and 50 grams each of processed angelica and fragrant wood. Remove hair from fragrant wood, and use five grams of asarum without seedlings, and one gram each of lotus leaf ash and frankincense ground separately, 50 grams of bitter neem broken into four pieces and stir-fried. Dragon brain and musk are ground separately at five grams each, and 250 grams of acid pomegranate peel. Grind into a fine powder, use five grams each time, brush as usual, and rinse with warm water, twice daily.[58p]
    Zhusha San: A fine powder for cleaning the teeth.
    Ground zhusha, fragrant grass, mint, clove, cyperus, sweet saposhnikovia, white atractylodes, rhizoma cimicifuga, and yellow dan (each one tael), pig's tooth soap pod (two taels), cold water stone (eight taels), plaster (four taels), white sandalwood, and zingiberis (each five qian). Grind into a fine powder and mix well; it’s excellent for cleaning the teeth.

    Miaoying San: Strengthens teeth, disperses wind, and regulates qi, benefiting black hair.
    Ginseng, fine xin (removed seedlings), white poria, and cyperus (fried to remove hair), chuanxiong, white tribulus (fried to remove corners), and cardamom (each five qian), prepared herbal decoction, white atractylodes, calcined plaster, and dragon bone (each six qian), with a little musk ground separately. Grind together into a fine powder; in the morning, rinse with warm water.

    Dihuang Wan: Treats loose teeth.
    White poria, ginseng, and shan zhu rou (each four taels), goji root (three taels), and raw d黄 (five jin, extract juice), white honey (one jin), and a little oil.     Sweet Dew Drink
    This remedy treats the internal heat in the stomach of men, women, and children, tooth decay, bad breath, swollen gums, pus and blood occasionally oozing out, drooping eyelids, a frequent desire to close the eyes, irritability with a loss of appetite; it also addresses red, swollen, and painful eyes not tolerating cooling medicine, sores in the mouth and on the tongue, swollen and painful throat, and skin rashes; it can be taken whether the rash has appeared or not.
    Ingredients:

    • Loquat leaves, brushed to remove hair
    • Dried, mature Rehmannia root
    • Venere Lustre (Asparagus root), heart removed and roasted
    • Dried bitter orange peel, pulp removed and stir-fried
    • Mountain artemisia (Chenopodium), stems removed
    • Dried Ophiopogon, heart removed and roasted
    • Dendrobium, roots removed
    • Honeyed licorice
    • Scutellaria baicalensis
    • Fresh Rehmannia root

    Grind the ingredients into a fine powder, take two qian (a measure) each time, mix with one bowl of water, boil down to seven-tenths, strain, and take warm after meals and before bed. For children, the dose should be divided into two parts, adjusting according to age.

    Five Spirit Ointment
    This remedy treats loose teeth.

    • Five Spirit resin, 5 qian
    • Pine resin, 1 liang
    • Yellow wax, 1 liang

    • Yellow cinnabar, 2 qian 5 fen

Every night, apply one piece to the gums; if there is saliva, it can be spat out, and swallowing will not be obstructed. This medication is used once at night; place it under a loosened tooth root, applying both inside and out, without causing too much discomfort.
